<analysis>**original_problem_statement:**
L'utilisateur a initialement demandé une application de calcul d'empreinte carbone. Les exigences ont évolué pour inclure un tableau de bord, la gestion des objectifs de réduction (SBTi), le versioning des facteurs d'émission, et un refactoring majeur.

Dans cette session, les demandes se sont concentrées sur :
1.  **Fonctionnalité d'export de données :** L'utilisateur a demandé un moyen d'extraire toutes les données de la base.
2.  **Import en masse :** L'utilisateur a fourni des fichiers JSON pour un import en masse des facteurs d'émission et des sous-catégories.
3.  **Amélioration de l'authentification :** L'utilisateur a demandé l'ajout de fonctionnalités de récupération de mot de passe.
4.  **Rapports de bugs multiples :**
    - La saisie de données n'impactait pas le bon exercice fiscal.
    - La gestion des utilisateurs (promotion/suppression) dans l'interface d'administration ne fonctionnait pas.
    - L'URL dans les emails de confirmation de compte était incorrecte.
    - La modification de l'appartenance d'une sous-catégorie à une catégorie ne se reflétait pas dans la saisie.
5.  **Refonte du Dashboard :** L'utilisateur a demandé une refonte de l'onglet Résultats du tableau de bord, en fournissant une maquette visuelle.

**PRODUCT REQUIREMENTS:**
-   Analyse du cycle de vie des produits.
-   Gestion des ventes de produits par exercice fiscal.
-   Archivage automatique des produits.
-   Dashboard & Rapports exportables (implémenté en JSON).
-   Panneau Admin pour gérer les facteurs d'émission, utilisateurs, etc.
-   Définition d'objectifs de réduction carbone (trajectoire SBTi).
-   Système d'authentification complet (récupération de mot de passe, etc.).
-   Import en masse de données de référence (facteurs, sous-catégories).

**User's preferred language**: Français

**what currently exists?**
Une application full-stack (React/FastAPI/MongoDB) fonctionnelle et auditée.
-   **Backend :**
    -   Un système d'authentification complet a été implémenté, incluant la récupération de mot de passe par email (via SMTP Infomaniak), le verrouillage de compte après échecs, la vérification d'email et l'option Se souvenir de moi.
    -   Une fonctionnalité d'export de données robuste via l'API () permet de télécharger des sauvegardes complètes ou des sous-ensembles de données (activités, produits, facteurs) en JSON.
    -   Un script a été utilisé pour importer en masse 1190 facteurs d'émission et 89 sous-catégories depuis des fichiers JSON fournis.
    -   Les API ont été corrigées pour refléter dynamiquement les changements d'association entre catégories et sous-catégories.
    -   La logique de création d'activité a été corrigée pour associer la nouvelle entrée à l'exercice fiscal sélectionné dans l'interface, et non à la date du jour.
    -   Les API de gestion des utilisateurs (promotion/suppression) ont été corrigées.
-   **Frontend :**
    -   La page d'administration a été améliorée avec un onglet Export fonctionnel et un onglet Utilisateurs permettant la suppression (avec confirmation) et la gestion des rôles.
    -   Les pages de récupération de mot de passe (, ) ont été créées et intégrées.
    -   La page d'authentification a été mise à jour avec une option Se souvenir de moi, un indicateur de force de mot de passe et un lien Mot de passe oublié ?.
    -   La page des facteurs d'émission a été mise à jour pour afficher correctement les facteurs au nouveau format (V2).
    -   L'onglet Résultats du tableau de bord a été remplacé par un nouveau composant  en vue d'une refonte.

**Last working item**:
    - Last item agent was working: Démarrage de la refonte de l'onglet Résultats du tableau de bord, suite à la demande de l'utilisateur avec une maquette visuelle. L'agent a créé un nouveau composant  et l'a intégré dans la page , en remplacement de l'ancien code.
    - Status: IN PROGRESS

    - User Testing Done: N

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/register'
params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/register': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/register?

        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238

        # handles RFC 3986 only.

            self.url = url
            return

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
E           requests.exceptions.MissingSchema: Invalid URL '/api/auth/login': No scheme supplied. Perhaps you meant https:///api/auth/login?

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:

self = <PreparedRequest [POST]>, url = '/api/auth/login', params = OrderedDict()

    def prepare_url(self, url, params):
        """Prepares the given HTTP URL."""
        #: Accept objects that have string representations.
        #: We're unable to blindly call unicode/str functions
        #: as this will include the bytestring indicator (b'')
        #: on python 3.x.
        #: https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/2238
        if isinstance(url, bytes):
            url = url.decode("utf8")
        else:
            url = str(url)
    
        # Remove leading whitespaces from url
        url = url.lstrip()
    
        # Don't do any URL preparation for non-HTTP schemes like `mailto`,
        # `data` etc to work around exceptions from `url_parse`, which
        # handles RFC 3986 only.
        if ":" in url and not url.lower().startswith("http"):
            self.url = url
            return
    
        # Support for unicode domain names and paths.
        try:
            scheme, auth, host, port, path, query, fragment = parse_url(url)
        except LocationParseError as e:
            raise InvalidURL(*e.args)
    
        if not scheme:
>           raise MissingSchema(
                f"Invalid URL {url!r}: No scheme supplied. "
                f"Perhaps you meant https://{url}?"
            )
